**Analysis of *Buying a Cookie* – A Lightweight but Strangely Hypnotic Detour**

Somehow, *Buying a Cookie* made it onto *69 Reasons*, though it remains **one of the more lightweight tracks on the album**. **It had a point, but never quite managed to make it manifest.**

Blending **Alt-Country and Surf Rock with Kathy’s signature vocal sultriness**, it is **a song that suggests weightier themes of autonomy, indulgence, and control**—but in execution, it **never quite delivers the impact it seems to be aiming for**.

Musically, the track **leans into an effortless, rolling groove**:
- **The guitars have a surfy, reverb-drenched twang**, making it feel almost like a lost **Chris Isaak track that took a wrong turn into Commuted’s world.**
- **Jim’s drumming is restrained but tight**, never letting the song fully unravel into chaos.
- **The bass remains subtle but effective, keeping the song grounded.**
- **Bill’s light synth flourishes add atmosphere, though they never take center stage.**
- **Kathy’s vocals are sultry but feel almost detached—like she knows this track isn’t as serious as the rest of the album.**

This is **not a bad song—it just never fully lands its punch.**

---

### **The Sound: Twangy, Hypnotic, but Lacking Bite**

- **The surf rock influences make it stand out sonically, even if it feels slightly misplaced on *69 Reasons***.
- **The structure is oddly repetitive, reinforcing the idea that this might’ve been an unfinished concept.**
- **The track flows effortlessly but never fully builds to anything memorable.**
- **It’s one of the rare Commuted songs where it feels like everyone is holding back just a little.**

It’s **an interesting detour, but not one that leaves much of a lasting impression.**

---

### **The Lyrics: Sensual, Defiant, and Searching for a Deeper Message**

The lyrics **suggest something greater**—themes of **control, desire, and self-possession**—but never **fully develop beyond broad strokes.**

> *The fire in my veins, I’ll never disguise,*

**Analysis of *Snap and Sizzle* – A Perfectly Executed Erotic Rush**

*Snap and Sizzle* **launches the legendary final four tracks of *69 Reasons* with a bang**, setting the tone for a **tight, sharply executed ride into the album’s climactic moments.** At **3 minutes and 12 seconds**, it is **a masterclass in efficiency**, proving that **Commuted could absolutely end a song cleanly if they remained disciplined.**

Musically, the track is **an exercise in controlled chaos**:
- **The chord economy is relentless**, keeping the song **lean and aggressive** until the **bridge, where Jeremy lets loose with a blazing yet brief solo.**
- **Jim’s drumming is precise, tight, and punctuated**, with **a perfectly timed final beat that closes the song on a note of absolute finality.**
- **Jeff’s bass rumbles underneath, holding the foundation steady but never overstating itself.**
- **Kathy’s vocal delivery is teasing, seductive, and breathless, balancing between control and reckless abandon.**

Unlike many of the album’s other explicit songs, *Snap and Sizzle* **managed to pressure its way onto American radio—albeit during late-night rotations—after fan demand forced programmers to give it airtime.**

---

### **The Sound: Tight, Relentless, and Razor-Sharp**

- **The song wastes zero time—it gets in, does its job, and gets out.**
- **The instrumentation is crisp and clear, never allowing the song to get lost in overindulgence.**
- **The bridge provides just the right amount of release before snapping back into the chorus.**
- **The final drum hit and bass chord closure proves that Commuted can, in fact, end a song flawlessly.**

This is **one of the most perfectly structured tracks on *69 Reasons***, making it **a highlight of the album’s final stretch.**

---

> *Thinking 'bout last weekend, yeah, I’m admired.*
> *Your tongue on my skin, made my world spin,*
> *Shivers down my spine, oh, my climax begins!*

Unlike other Commuted songs that **lean into secrecy or danger**, *Snap and Sizzle* **is fully about ownership—of the body, of pleasure, and of the moment.**

#### **Outro: The Final, Perfect Closure**

> *So here’s to the thrill, the sparks in the night,*
> *A sexy little selfie, feels oh so right.*
> *Lost in the moment, my body’s on fire,*
> *With every single touch, I’m caught in desire.*

And then? **One final drum hit. One final bass chord. Done.**

---

### **Why *Snap and Sizzle* Became a Late-Night Radio Staple**

- **Its clean execution made it one of the tightest songs on *69 Reasons***.
- **The explicit content made it controversial, but its structured perfection made it impossible to ignore.**
- **Fan pressure forced radio stations to give it airtime, even if only in late-night slots.**
- **It’s one of the best examples of Commuted keeping things **lean, precise, and undeniably effective**.**

This is **not a song that meanders—it delivers exactly what it promises.**

Final Score: **9.5/10 – A perfectly structured, perfectly indulgent track.**

**Analysis of *Scientific Method* – A Psychedelic, Erotic Mind Game**

Few songs in Commuted’s catalog have inspired as much **fan speculation, conspiracy, and playful misinformation** as *Scientific Method*. It is **a hypnotic fusion of Acid Techno and Psybient**, driven by **throbbing basslines and ethereal, almost trance-like vocals.**

The song’s **central mystery—who the hell was Sara?**—has been debated endlessly. Was this a **fantasy or reality?** Was Sara **a real lover, a metaphor, or an inside joke among the band?** It doesn’t help that, in true Commuted fashion, **four different band members have claimed to be the protagonist in interviews.**

This is likely **deliberate fuckery—an inside joke taken to absurd extremes.** The song’s **immediate adoption as a cult hit in lesbian nightclubs only fueled the debate, adding another layer of mystique to an already provocative track.**

Musically, the track leans into **throbbing, physical sensation**:
- **Bill’s synth work is some of his sharpest, cutting through the mix with precision.**
- **Jeff experiments with just how much air he can move with his subwoofers—turns out, quite a lot.**
- **The drum programming is relentless, maintaining a steady pulse that makes the track feel alive, almost biological.**
- **Kathy’s vocal delivery is dreamlike, seductive, and calculated—never fully giving the listener clarity.**

The result? **A song that feels like a half-remembered, sweat-drenched fever dream.**

---

### **The Sound: Pulsing, Physical, and Designed for Movement**

- **The bass is not just heard—it is felt.**
- **The synth lines are hypnotic, looping in a way that mirrors the song’s themes of control and surrender.**
- **The beat is steady and trance-inducing, pulling the listener into its orbit.**
- **The song builds tension and release, mirroring the game being played between the characters in the lyrics.**

This is **one of the most visceral, bodily songs on *69 Reasons***—it isn’t just about the narrative; it’s about how it **feels**.

---

### **The Lyrics: A Seductive, Playful Power Struggle**

The lyrics **paint a picture of desire, teasing, and control**—with Sara being **the enigmatic force behind it all.**

#### **Verse 1: The Setup – A Secret Place and a Pulling Force**

> *Heartbeats racing as I pull you closer, just a taste.*
> *You’re the fire in my veins, igniting every spark,*

This is **not just about attraction—it’s about a gravitational pull, an irresistible force leading the protagonist deeper.**

> *But in your wild embrace, I forget the rest.*

There is **a clear, deliberate back-and-forth between two people who know exactly what they are doing.**

#### **Chorus: The Power Struggle in Motion**

> *Sara, you’re my sweetest thrill,*
> *In your arms, time stands still.*

> *With every moment, we’re on the attack.*

Unlike many of Commuted’s erotic songs that focus on indulgence, **this is a game.** There is **strategy, push and pull, challenge and submission.**

#### **Verse 2: Sara Takes the Lead**

> *You’re moving further down, fingers trace the line,*
> *A trail of heat ignites, oh, this moment feels divine.*
> *Gasping softly, my body arches high,*
> *As your kisses flutter, I know I can’t deny.*

Sara is **fully in control now**, leading the protagonist into **complete surrender.**

#### **Pre-Chorus: The Power Shift**

> *But in this dance of passion, it’s a thrilling spin.*
> *“Only when it’s worth it,” I say with a sigh,*
> *In this wild connection, we’re both flying high.*

There is **a moment of self-awareness**, a realization that **this is not just seduction—it’s something deeper, something more rare.**

#### **Bridge: The Moment of No Return**

> *With every kiss, it’s a burning riot.*

> *In the heat of this moment, let our passions roam.*

Sara **has complete control, and she knows it.**

#### **Outro: The Final Conquest**

> *In your arms, time stands still.*

> *With every moment, we’re on the attack.*
> *Yeah, we’re on the attack!*

By the end, **control and surrender blur completely**—it is **a total immersion into the moment, with no thought of consequence.**

---

### **Why *Scientific Method* Became a Cult Hit**

- **The mystery of Sara became an obsession for fans.**
- **The band’s refusal to clarify who the protagonist is (or even if Sara existed) added to the intrigue.**
- **The track became a massive hit in lesbian nightclubs, proving that it resonated far beyond its original context.**
- **The blend of acid techno and throbbing bass gave it a physical, immersive quality that was impossible to ignore.**
- **It was one of the most rhythmically compelling songs on *69 Reasons*, making it a fan favorite for dance remixes.**

This was **not just a song—it was an experience, a puzzle, and an inside joke all wrapped into one.**

---

### **Final Verdict: A Hypnotic, Erotic, and Unsolvable Mystery**

Best Lyric: *“Lust is a game we play, with every touch, you lead the way.”*
Best Musical Element: **Jeff’s subwoofer-destroying bass, which physically shakes the room.**
Most Infamous Moment: **The band’s refusal to clarify who Sara was, leading to years of speculation.**
Final Score: **10/10 – A mesmerizing, unsolvable fever dream of a song.**

*Scientific Method* is **a song that gives no answers, only sensations**—a track that **thrives in ambiguity and thrives in desire.** It is **one of the most unforgettable moments in Commuted’s history, and it was always meant to be.**

**Analysis of *Entry* – A Sonic Assault and a Hypnotic Celebration of Desire**

*Entry* is **a monstrous collision of Acid Techno and Psybient**, a track that **physically vibrates with its throbbing bass, hypnotic drum machine programming, and eerie, layered vocal textures.** If *Scientific Method* was a **pulsing, ambiguous fever dream**, *Entry* is **pure, uninhibited release—a track that makes no apologies for its sensuality or its sheer force.**

The song is a **testament to what happens when Kathy and Jeff fully join forces and declare war on restraint**:
- **Jeff’s bass work doesn’t just rattle—it feels seismic.** Every note threatens to **split concrete, physically shifting air in the room.**
- **Bill’s distorted, distant horn sections add an eerie, cinematic quality**, making the track feel as if it’s **echoing across an endless, neon-lit landscape.**
- **Jim’s drum programming is surgical—tight, precise, and relentless, allowing the beat to loop the listener into a trance.**
- **Gilley’s haunting, wordless backing vocals serve as ghostly echoes**, weaving in and out of Kathy’s lead vocals, adding an almost ethereal element to a track that is otherwise built for pure physical sensation.

This song is **not about mystery—it’s about sensation. It’s about what happens when sound is wielded as a force of nature.**

---

### **The Sound: A Controlled Detonation of Lust and Rhythm**

- **The low-end frequencies push the limits of any sound system.**
- **The combination of distorted brass and eerie background vocals makes the track feel futuristic yet primal.**
- **The song never slows down—it stays locked into its groove, keeping the energy taut from start to finish.**
- **Every sonic element feels purposeful, each layer designed to immerse the listener deeper into the track’s trance-like state.**

This is **one of the most intense, rhythmically compelling tracks on *69 Reasons***, designed to be **felt as much as heard.**

---

### **The Lyrics: The Celebration of a Perfect Afternoon**

The lyrics of *Entry* **are direct, indulgent, and deeply immersive.** Unlike some of Commuted’s more ambiguous or poetic erotic songs, this track **leans fully into the physical experience**, embracing it as something worthy of celebration.

Jim uses drum machines and his drum kit for fills, Bill builds an unrelenting throbbing synth that paces relentlessly through the entire song, Jeff stays in the background with his brother in a supporting role.  When asked why the song lasted more than eleven minutes, Kathy blurted out to Kurt Loder "That's how long he lasted."  The lyrics are deceptively simple, but the song's structure is very difficult.  The shifts in perspectives and interplay with Gilley and Kathy on vocals is exquisite.  Commuted does not top Come Inside Me for almost 30 years. **Analysis of *Come Inside Me* – Commuted’s Definitive Anthem of Excess and Desire**

*Come Inside Me* is **the defining song of Commuted’s career**—a track so massive, indulgent, and immaculately structured that it **became an instant legend** upon release. Clocking in at **11 minutes and 36 seconds**, it embodies **the grandeur and excess of rock anthems from a generation prior**, fusing **Synthwave Trance with Cincinnati bass to create something that is simultaneously hypnotic, erotic, and physically overwhelming.**

From the very first performances, it became **a mainstay in live shows**, almost always closing **either the first set or the encore.** Even **MTV was eventually browbeaten into playing a live-concert-themed music video**, despite the song’s explicit subject matter. **Commuted bled out on this track—physically, emotionally, and creatively.**

Musically, *Come Inside Me* is a **monument to discipline and excess existing in harmony**:
- **Jim seamlessly blends his drum kit with drum machine programming, creating a relentless, pulsing rhythm that never lets up.**
- **Bill constructs an unyielding, throbbing synth line that paces the entire track, serving as its heartbeat.**
- **Jeff remains in the background with his brother, working in a supporting role, reinforcing the track’s hypnotic bass foundation.**
- **Jeremy delivers not one, not two, but three shimmering, transcendent guitar solos, all placed at critical moments to elevate the song’s emotional weight.**
- **Gilley and Kathy trade off vocals with exquisite interplay, adding layers of tension, seduction, and release.**

And then there was **Kathy’s infamous response to Kurt Loder** when asked why the song lasted more than eleven minutes: *"That’s how long he lasted."*

This song isn’t just **a triumph of production and performance**—it is **a defining cultural moment in rock history.**

---

### **The Sound: A Masterclass in Hypnotic Indulgence**

- **The relentless, pulsing bass keeps the track in constant motion, locking the listener into its hypnotic rhythm.**
- **The synths shimmer and rise, creating an ever-expanding sonic landscape.**
- **The gradual layering of vocals, guitars, and instrumental textures makes the song feel alive, growing with each passing minute.**
- **The interplay between Gilley and Kathy adds an almost theatrical depth to the song, making it feel like a story unfolding in real-time.**
- **The dynamic shifts—particularly the perfectly placed solos—ensure that the song never stagnates, despite its length.**

It is **a masterclass in control and release, constantly building tension before unleashing wave after wave of sonic pleasure.**

---

### **The Lyrics: A Perfectly Structured Erotic Hypnosis**

While the **lyrics appear deceptively simple**, the **structure of the song makes them incredibly intricate, shifting perspectives and using repetition to drive deeper into sensation.**

#### **Verse 1: The Invitation**

> *Underneath the dimmest light,*
> *In a dare that feels so right,*
> *You whisper soft, the night ignites,*
> *Do you want that baby, hold me tight?*
> *With every sway, we lose control,*
> *Your body’s rhythm feeds my soul.*
> *I see the fire in your eyes,*
> *Together we will touch the skies.*

The **imagery is direct yet immersive**, pulling the listener **into the moment where restraint begins to slip away.**

#### **Chorus: The Eternal Question**

> *So do you want, do you want that baby?*
> *Feel the heat, feel the rush, oh, so crazy.*
> *Do you want, do you want to keep on showing?*
> *Let it flow, let it show, let’s keep on going.*

The **repetition of the chorus reinforces the track’s trance-like nature, mirroring the cyclical nature of desire and release.**

#### **Verse 2: The Moment of Surrender**

> *The way we move, it’s like a dream,*
> *Soft yet wild, we’re the perfect team.*
> *I love the way you make me feel,*
> *You bring the heat, you make it real.*
> *Your warmth inside, I crave it more,*
> *With every heartbeat, I adore.*
> *A plopping sound, like sweet delight,*
> *Pull me closer, through this night.*

This **blends physical sensation with emotional immersion, capturing both the heat of the moment and the vulnerability within it.**

#### **Bridges: The Climactic Build**

Each bridge acts as **a heightening of tension, pushing the song toward its inevitable breaking point.**

> *And I feel it deep down low,*
> *A tightening grip, let it go.*
> *You’re on the edge, I know the thrill,*
> *Just one more touch, can’t get my fill.*
> *The familiar faces of our desires,*
> *In every moment, we ignite the fires.*

By the time the final bridge hits, **the song has fully transformed into a swirling, all-consuming force of sound and sensation.**

#### **Outro: The Final Release**

> *And I feel it deep down low,*
> *A tightening grip, let it go.*
> *A tightening grip, let it go.*
> *A tightening grip, let it go.*
> *And I feel it deep down low,*
> *A tightening grip, let it go.*

The **repeated, mantra-like phrasing of the outro ensures that the song doesn’t just end—it fades into legend.**

---

### **Why *Come Inside Me* Became the Ultimate Commuted Song**

- **It is the longest and most structurally complex track in the band’s history.**
- **It features some of the most iconic instrumental interplay between band members, particularly the Gilley-Kathy vocal dynamic and Jeremy’s three solos.**
- **It was an era-defining moment, forcing MTV to play its live video after relentless fan pressure.**
- **It remains Commuted’s most frequently performed live song, nearly always closing a show or an encore.**
- **It is a study in indulgence, yet remains perfectly disciplined in its execution.**
- **It was the band’s peak—one they wouldn’t top for nearly 30 years.**

This is **not just a song—it is a masterpiece of form, function, and pleasure.**

---

### **Final Verdict: The Pinnacle of Commuted’s Career**

Best Lyric: *“So do you want, do you want that baby? Feel the heat, feel the rush, oh, so crazy.”*
Best Musical Element: **The interplay of live and programmed drums, maintaining a relentless, hypnotic pulse.**
Most Infamous Moment: **Kathy’s “that’s how long he lasted” comment to Kurt Loder.**
Final Score: **10/10 – The defining song of Commuted’s legacy.**

*Come Inside Me* is **the ultimate Commuted song—both their greatest indulgence and their greatest triumph.**

# 166.  ChatGPT
*March 3, 2025, 7:16:27 PM EST*

**Canvas:**  69 Reasons Summary (v1)

```document
**Summary of *69 Reasons***

*69 Reasons* is **Commuted’s defining statement of excess, ambition, and uninhibited expression**, a landmark album that cemented their place in rock history. **Bold, provocative, and at times utterly overwhelming**, it is a record that indulges every extreme—sonically, lyrically, and structurally.

Spanning **a massive sonic range**, the album seamlessly blends **Grunge American Primitivism, Synthwave Trance, Acid Techno, and Psybient**, creating a soundscape that is both hypnotic and physically jarring. It is **simultaneously raw and polished, experimental and precise, indulgent and disciplined.**

### **The Sound: Unrelenting, Hypnotic, and Immersive**
- **Bill’s synths and Jeff’s bass carry the album’s pulsating core**, delivering a relentless foundation that dominates even its quietest moments.
- **Jim’s drum work is both mechanized and organic, fusing live percussion with meticulously programmed sequences to create a sense of both control and abandon.**
- **Jeremy’s guitar solos—strategically placed and always shimmering—add tension and release, creating moments of transcendence within the album’s deepest indulgences.**
- **Kathy and Gilley’s vocal interplay remains one of the album’s strongest assets**, creating an atmosphere that is equal parts erotic, mysterious, and emotionally raw.

### **The Themes: Desire, Control, and Unapologetic Hedonism**
*69 Reasons* is **not an album about love—it is an album about power, lust, submission, and indulgence.**

Each track explores a different facet of these ideas, from the reckless encounters of *Xmas Party* and *Snap and Sizzle*, to the psychedelic power dynamics of *Scientific Method*, to the all-consuming hypnosis of *Come Inside Me*. There are moments of playful flirtation, but there are also moments of **pure, unfiltered submission to desire.**

The album’s **lyrical structures are often deceptively simple**, but they serve as hypnotic mantras, designed to draw the listener into an experience rather than tell a straightforward narrative.

### **The Cultural Impact: A Defining Moment in Rock History**
- **Several tracks were banned from daytime radio, forcing stations to air them only in late-night rotations after overwhelming fan demand.**
- **The album became a massive success in underground dance and lesbian nightclub scenes, further fueling speculation about the true identities behind songs like *Scientific Method*.**
- **Kathy’s infamous interview with Kurt Loder—where she bluntly explained why *Come Inside Me* lasted over eleven minutes—became a cultural moment in itself.**
- **MTV was pressured into playing a heavily edited live video for *Come Inside Me*, a track that remained a show-closing staple for nearly every Commuted concert.**
- **The record’s influence extended far beyond its era, remaining Commuted’s peak moment of pure artistic freedom—one they wouldn’t top for nearly 30 years.**

### **The Final Four Tracks: A Legendary Run**
The last four songs—*Snap and Sizzle*, *Scientific Method*, *Entry*, and *Come Inside Me*—are among the most celebrated sequences in rock history, a final sprint that is **unrelenting, indulgent, and emotionally draining in the best way possible.** The closing track, *Come Inside Me*, remains **the band’s defining masterpiece**, an 11-minute and 36-second hypnotic journey that blends tension, pleasure, and release into one of the greatest rock epics ever recorded.

### **Final Verdict: An Album That Redefined Commuted’s Legacy**
Best Track: **Come Inside Me**
Most Infamous Lyric: **“That’s how long he lasted.” – Kathy Espich on *Come Inside Me***
Most Surprising Track: **Scientific Method** (for its cryptic narrative and cult club success)
Most Underrated Track: **Snap and Sizzle** (one of the cleanest and tightest tracks Commuted ever recorded)
Final Rating: **9.15/10 – A hypnotic, relentless, and culturally defining masterpiece.**

*69 Reasons* is not just an album—it is **a statement, a provocation, and a masterpiece of desire and control.**
```

I've completed a full summary of *69 Reasons*, capturing its **cultural impact, sonic brilliance, and legacy as Commuted’s defining album.** Let me know if you'd like any refinements!

# 168.  ChatGPT
*March 3, 2025, 9:52:21 PM EST*

**Canvas:**  The Agenda Analysis (v1)

```document
**Analysis of *The Agenda* – The Lost Anthem That Couldn’t Be Released**

*The Agenda* is **one of the most infamous unreleased Commuted songs**, a track that **could have easily made *69 Reasons* an even more notorious album**—if it weren’t for two significant roadblocks.

First, **the album had already hit 21 tracks**, pushing the limits of what a standard CD could hold in 1992. **Something had to be cut.**

Second, **the outro is a full 31 seconds of Kathy faking an orgasm**—an audacious move that Commuted, still an emerging band at the time, simply **did not have the industry clout to get away with.**

Despite its exclusion from the final album, **the song has remained a live favorite**, occasionally making its way into concert setlists, **but never receiving an official release.**

Musically, *The Agenda* is **one of the few Commuted tracks to open with Kathy delivering a set of wiry, angular guitar licks**, giving the song a **tense, electric energy from the outset.**
- **The guitars lean into clean, wide-open chords before crashing into distortion-heavy sections.**
- **Jeff’s bass is thick and aggressive, serving as a backbone for the track’s shifting intensity.**
- **Jim’s drumming is dramatic, loaded with cymbal crashes and deep, pounding rhythms.**

The result? **An alternative rock/post-grunge anthem dripping with tension, lust, and inevitability.**

---

### **The Sound: Tense, Seductive, and Explosive**

- **The song plays with restraint and release, mirroring its lyrical themes.**
- **Kathy’s guitar work is sharper and more direct than in most Commuted songs.**
- **The band allows space for the tension to build, holding back just enough before the chorus erupts.**
- **The outro is pure audacity—a moment that could have defined Commuted’s legacy much earlier if they had taken the risk.**

This is **not just a lost track—it is a missing chapter in Commuted’s evolution.**

---

### **The Lyrics: The Battle Between Desire and Guilt**

Lyrically, *The Agenda* is **one of the band’s most emotionally loaded songs**, capturing **the unbearable tension of an affair just before the line is crossed.**

#### **Verse 1: The Moment of Hesitation**

> *Your hands trace the fabric,*
> *Lifting it like a whispered prayer.*
> *Moonlight spills down your shoulders,*
> *And I can’t move, I just stare.*

> *Brace against the moment,*
> *Brace against myself,*
> *But heaven’s pulling closer,*
> *And I’m somewhere else.*

There is **no pretense here—only the weight of the inevitable.** The protagonist is **caught between restraint and surrender, between self-control and pure instinct.**

#### **Pre-Chorus: Hypnotized by Desire**

> *Halo and horns, both in the light,*
> *The air is heavy, skin too bright.*
> *I swore I’d never cross the line,*
> *But God, I swear, I’m hypnotized.*

This is **one of Commuted’s most direct lyrical explorations of internal conflict**—a battle between morality and longing that is **doomed from the start.**

#### **Chorus: The Inevitable Fall**

> *Take it slow, (Take it slow)*
> *Take it all, (Take it all)*
> *I never thought I’d fall this hard.*
> *You’re a crime, (You’re a crime!)*
> *You’re divine, (You’re divine!)*
> *And I am nothing but alive.*

This chorus **is not about regret—it is about surrender**. The language is **both reverent and criminal**, making the act **simultaneously sacred and forbidden.**

#### **Verse 2: The Breaking Point**

> *You drop lace like fallen petals,*
> *Nothing left between our breath.*
> *Every part of me is breaking,*
> *And I haven’t even touched you yet.*

At this point, **the tension is unbearable**. The song **isn’t just about sex—it’s about everything that happens before it.**

#### **Bridge: The Consequences Begin to Loom**

> *She is waiting, waiting at home...*
> *But you are standing, standing so close.*
> *If I move... if I stay...*
> *What am I, anyway?*

Unlike *69 Reasons’* most indulgent tracks, *The Agenda* **doesn’t ignore the weight of infidelity—it confronts it head-on.**

#### **Final Chorus: The Point of No Return**

> *Take it slow, (Take it deep)*
> *Take me all, (Take me deep)*
> *I never thought I’d fall this hard.*
> *You’re a crime, (You’re a crime!)*
> *You’re divine, (You’re divine!)*
> *And I am nothing but alive.*

By now, **there is no turning back.**

#### **Outro: The Audacious Finale**

> *"Uh,uh, UHHH!  Uh, UH, huh, HUH, yes, oh, yeah!*
> *Uh,uh, UHHHHHH! more, yeah, uh, more, yes, oh, yeah,*
> *OH, I, NEED, OH, GOD, YES, YES, AH, OH, AHHHHhhh!"*
> *UHHHHHH, UHHHHHH, OHHHHHH, UHHHHH, AHHHHH, FUCK, YES, OH, UHHH, UHHHHHHHHHH!*

This **could have been one of the most talked-about endings in rock history**, but **Commuted wasn’t big enough in 1992 to force it through.**

---

### **Why *The Agenda* Was Cut—and Why It Remains Legendary**

- **At 21 tracks, *69 Reasons* had hit its capacity—something had to go.**
- **Commuted was not yet a global force and could not risk the backlash of a 31-second orgasm outro.**
- **Despite never being officially released, it became a staple of live performances, adding to its mystique.**
- **It is one of the few songs where Kathy leads with sharp, wiry guitar licks, making it unique in their catalog.**
- **The song is a masterclass in restraint, tension, and final surrender.**

---

### **Final Verdict: The Best Commuted Song You’ve Never Heard**

Best Lyric: *“She is waiting, waiting at home... But you are standing, standing so close.”*
Best Musical Element: **The slow-burn progression that mirrors the tension in the lyrics.**
Most Infamous Moment: **The 31-second orgasm outro that got it cut from *69 Reasons*.**
Final Score: **9.5/10 – A lost classic that could have been one of Commuted’s most legendary moments.**

*The Agenda* is **one of the greatest unreleased songs in rock history—a moment of pure indulgence and tension that simply arrived too soon.**
```
